RNA was extracted using TRIzol (Life Technologies) or PureLink (ThermoFisher) kits, DNAse-treated using the DNA-free™ Kit (Life Technologies), and RNA quality was assessed by Nanodrop (ThermoFisher), agarose gel, and BioAnalyzer (Agilent). Strand-specific libraries were prepared using the Illumina TruSeq kit, and library quality was checked by BioAnalyzer (Agilent). Libraries were sequenced using Illumina technology. The average number of total mapped paired-end reads ranged from ~60 to ~100 million reads.</p><p>Raw RNA-seq reads were filtered and trimmed using BBDuk (v37) from the BBtools package (v. 38.0)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Bushnell, B. BBMap. &#xA;https://sourceforge.net/projects/bbmap&#xA;&#xA; (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d18949e3752">80</a></sup>. Reads were aligned to the complete reference genome (ABR113 v. 1.0) using BBmap (v37)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Bushnell, B. BBMap. &#xA;https://sourceforge.net/projects/bbmap&#xA;&#xA; (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d18949e3756">80</a></sup>. To increase mapping stringency, reads were required to share 90% sequence identity with the target location, and ambiguous reads were discarded. With these criteria, more than 96% of reads were mapped unambiguously. There were ~194 genes, which were associated with five or more ambiguous reads. Gene-level counts were obtained using HTSeq (v. 0.9.1)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Bushnell, B. BBMap. &#xA;https://sourceforge.net/projects/bbmap&#xA;&#xA; (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d18949e3760">80</a></sup>. Transcripts per million (TPM) values were calculated using a custom Python script.</p><p>To test for homeolog-expression bias using DESeq2 v. 1.24.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Love, M. I., Huber, W. &amp; Anders, S. Moderated estimation of fold change and dispersion for RNA-seq data with DESeq2. Genome Biol. 15, 550 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d18949e3767">81</a></sup>, each library was split into two, with each subgenome of each library becoming one sample. Homeologs were determined using Phytozome’s Phytomine pipeline, incorporating both homology and synteny<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Goodstein, D. M. et al. Phytozome: a comparative platform for green plant genomics. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, D1178–D1186 (2012)." href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d18949e3771">82</a></sup>. Genes lacking a 1:1 homeolog were excluded from the DESeq2 analysis. The length of each homeolog was added to the DESeqDataSet using avgTxLength. This lengths matrix was incorporated into normalization factor estimation, which is in turn used to estimate each gene’s true expression value. The normalization factor option was designed mainly to account for differences in alternative transcript usage between conditions, but can be used to control for any known systematic bias for a given gene between two samples. Our models for the likelihood ratio test (using Wilkinson notation) were: full=library+subgenome, and reduced=library, so library was essentially handled as a batch effect.</p><p>Our candidate pseudogene identification protocol was based on the method of Session<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Session, A. M. et al. Genome evolution in the allotetraploid frog Xenopus laevis. Nature 538, 336–343 (2016)." href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d18949e3778">83</a></sup>. <i>Brachypodium hybridum</i> subgenomes were compared with their cognate diploid genomes three genes at a time to identify triplets where the central gene lacked a <i>B. hybridum</i> ortholog but the two flanking genes each had a syntenic <i>B. hybridum</i> ortholog. The <i>B. hybridum</i> genomic region between the two flanking orthologs was extracted using bedtools (v2.27.1)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Quinlan, A. R. BEDTools: the Swiss-army tool for genome feature analysis. Curr. Protoc. Bioinform. 47, 11. 12. 1–11. 12. 34 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d18949e3795">84</a></sup>, and the diploid gene was aligned to this sequence using the codon- and intron-aware protein2genome model of exonerate (v. 2.4.0) (<a href="https://www.ebi.ac.uk/about/vertebrate-genomics/software/exonerate">https://www.ebi.ac.uk/about/vertebrate-genomics/software/exonerate</a>). Alignments were parsed with the Biopython (v. 1.7.0) package ExonerateIO. RNA-seq counts were obtained strictly for the aligned regions using the customizable functionalities of HTSeq, and normalized by the total number of mapped reads for each library. Pairwise nonsynonymous to synonymous substitution rate ratios were calculated using the yn00 program from PAML (v. 4.9 h)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 85" title="Yang, Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol. Biol. Evol. 24, 1586–1591 (2007)." href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#ref-CR85" id="ref-link-section-d18949e3803">85</a></sup>. Finally, candidate pseudogenes were required to have a nonsynonymous to synonymous substitution rate ratio (dN/dS) of 0.5 or higher, and the log ratio of diploid to polyploid expression for the aligned region had to be &gt;0.3.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec30">Reporting summary</h3><p>Further information on research design is available in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#MOESM3">Nature Research Life Sciences Reporting Summary</a> linked to this article.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>Data supporting the findings of this work are available within the paper and its <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#MOESM1">Supplementary Information</a> files. A reporting summary for this Article is available as a Supplementary Information file. The datasets generated and analyzed during the current study are available from the corresponding author upon request. Genome assemblies and annotations can be downloaded from Phytozome [<a href="https://phytozome.jgi.doe.gov/">https://phytozome.jgi.doe.gov/</a>]. The direct link for the <i>B. hybridum</i> ABR113 reference genome is <a href="https://phytozome-next.jgi.doe.gov/info/Bhybridum_v1_1">https://phytozome-next.jgi.doe.gov/info/Bhybridum_v1_1</a>; the direct link for the <i>B. stacei</i> ABR114 reference genome is <a href="https://phytozome-next.jgi.doe.gov/info/Bstacei_v1_1">https://phytozome-next.jgi.doe.gov/info/Bstacei_v1_1</a>; and the direct link for the <i>B. distachyon</i> Bd21 reference genome is <a href="https://phytozome-next.jgi.doe.gov/info/Bdistachyon_v3_1">https://phytozome-next.jgi.doe.gov/info/Bdistachyon_v3_1</a>. The other genome assemblies and annotations created in this study (listed in Supplementary Data 1) can be downloaded from the <i>B. hybridum</i> genome page [<a href="https://phytozome-next.jgi.doe.gov/info/Bhybridum_v1_1">https://phytozome-next.jgi.doe.gov/info/Bhybridum_v1_1</a>] through the download directory labeled “Additional genomes used in Gordon et al. <i>Nat. Commun.</i> 2020” direct link <a href="https://genome.jgi.doe.gov/portal/pages/dynamicOrganismDownload.jsf?organism=Bhybridum">https://genome.jgi.doe.gov/portal/pages/dynamicOrganismDownload.jsf?organism=Bhybridum</a>. Note that a free account is required to download the data from Phytozome. The raw reads for the genomic sequences and RNA sequences are available from NCBI or ENA. The samples numbers, accessions, and hyperlinks are provided in Supplementary Data <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#MOESM8">4</a> and 9. Seeds for the lines used in this study are available from the USDA National Plant Germplasm Service or by request from the authors.The source data underlying Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#Fig6">6</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#Fig7">7</a>, and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#Fig8">8</a> and Supplementary Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#MOESM1">9</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#MOESM1">11</a>, and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5#MOESM1">12</a> are provided as a Source Data file.</p>

                        <span class="c-article-identifiers"><a class="c-article-identifiers__item" href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=search&amp;term=John P.+Vogel" data-track="click" data-track-action="author link - pubmed" data-track-label="link">PubMed</a><span class="u-hide"> </span><a class="c-article-identifiers__item" href="http://scholar.google.co.uk/scholar?as_q=&amp;num=10&amp;btnG=Search+Scholar&amp;as_epq=&amp;as_oq=&amp;as_eq=&amp;as_occt=any&amp;as_sauthors=%22John P.+Vogel%22&amp;as_publication=&amp;as_ylo=&amp;as_yhi=&amp;as_allsubj=all&amp;hl=en" data-track="click" data-track-action="author link - scholar" data-track-label="link">Google Scholar</a></span></p></div></div></li></ol></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="contributions">Contributions</h3><p>S.P.G. led the project, genome assembly, gene annotation, genetic mapping, directed k-mer and synteny and whole-genome alignment analyses, and coordinated collaborations and co-wrote initial draft; B.C.M. created the pan-genome; J.J.L. conducted k-mer and synteny and whole-genome alignment analyses and supported phylogenomic analyses; A.D. and A.C.E. sequenced Bd28 genome and transcriptome; V.S.T. conducted expression analysis and genetic mapping; V.R.S. performed expression analysis; A.S. and D.R. conducted preliminary k-mer analysis, and provided guidance and interpretation of genome evolution; J.M. carried out reference-based analysis; A.C., V.H.D.T., and B.C. performed RNA-seq experiments; A.K. did curation of genetic map; E.G., J.J., C.P., and J.S. conducted genome assembly; K.B. managed and coordinated all sequencing activities; A.D.P. and R.S. performed selection, population, and plastome analysis; J.L., E.W., and R.H. carried out cytogenetic analysis; C.N., J.H.D., and L.M. provided transcriptomics and germplasm; S.H. and S.L. <i>B. distachyon</i> sequencing; S.S. conducted annotation and D.G. carried out phytozome implementation; P.C. co-directed overall project, collected germplasm, led plastome and phylogenomic analysis, and co-wrote initial draft; J.P.V. conceived and directed overall project, co-wrote initial draft, analyzed pan-genome and reference analysis data. All authors reviewed and contributed to writing the paper.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding authors</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to
                <a id="corresp-c1" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5/email/correspondent/c1/new">Pilar Catalan</a> or <a id="corresp-c2" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5/email/correspondent/c2/new">John P. Vogel</a>.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="ethics" data-title="Ethics declarations"><div class="c-article-section" id="ethics-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="ethics">Ethics declarations</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="ethics-content">

                    <i>Nat Commun</i> <b>11, </b>3670 (2020). https://doi.org/10.1038/s41467-020-17302-5</p><p class="c-bibliographic-information__download-citation u-hide-print"><a data-test="citation-link" data-track="click" data-track-action="download article citation" data-track-label="link" data-track-external="" href="/articles/s41467-020-17302-5.ris">Download citation<svg width="16" height="16" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#global-icon-download"></use></svg></a></p><ul class="c-bibliographic-information__list" data-test="publication-history"><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item"><p>Received<span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><time datetime="2019-09-13">13 September 2019</time></span></p></li><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item"><p>Accepted<span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><time datetime="2020-06-19">19 June 2020</time></span></p></li><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item"><p>Published<span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><time datetime="2020-07-29">29 July 2020</time></span></p></li><li class="c-bibliographic-information__list-item c-bibliographic-information__list-item--doi"><p><abbr title="Digital Object Identifier">DOI</abbr><span class="u-hide">: </span><span class="c-bibliographic-information__value"><a href="https://doi.org/10.1038/s41467-020-17302-5" data-track="click" data-track-action="view doi" data-track-label="link" itemprop="sameAs">https://doi.org/10.1038/s41467-020-17302-5</a></span></p></li></ul><div data-component="share-box"></div><div data-component="article-info-list"></div></div></div></div></div></section>
